															 									<h2 class="blog-single-title">Java Swing Tutorial</h2>
								 							
 							


							<div class="single-social-section">

							<div class="mk-single-content" itemprop="mainContentOfPage">
								<p></p>
<div style="width:672px;padding:0;margin:5px;">
<div style="float:right;width:336px;">

<p><span class="style10">This site contains brief tutorials for java swing programming along with java swing examples and source code.</span></p>
<h2 class="style1"><span style="font-size: small;">Java Swings Tutorial</span></h2>
<p>What is <strong>Swings in java</strong> ?</p>
<ul>
<li>A part of The JFC</li>
<li><strong>Swing Java </strong>consists of<br />
Look and feel<br />
Accessibility<br />
Java 2D<br />
Drag and Drop, etc</li>
</ul>
<ul>
<ul>
<li><span class="style4">Compiling &amp; running programs</span></li>
</ul>
</ul>
<p><strong>javac</strong> &lt;program.java&gt; &amp;&amp; <strong> java</strong> &lt;program&gt;<br />
Or JCreator / IDE</p>
<ul>
<ul>
<li>if you do not explicitly add a GUI component to a container, the GUI component will not be displayed when the container appears on the screen.</li>
</ul>
</ul>
<p align="left">Swing, which is an extension library to the AWT, includes new and improved components that enhance the look and functionality of GUIs. Swing can be used to build Standalone swing gui Apps as well as Servlets and Applets. It employs a model/view design architecture. Swing is more portable and more flexible than AWT.</p>
<p><span class="style11"> <span style="font-weight: 400; text-decoration: underline;">Swing Model/view design:</span> </span>The &#8220;view part&#8221; of the MV design is implemented with a component object and the UI object. The &#8220;model part&#8221; of the MV design is implemented by a model object and a change listener object.</p>
<p>Swing is built on top of AWT and is entirely written in Java, using AWT&#8217;s lightweight component support. In particular, unlike AWT, t he architecture of Swing components makes it easy to customize both their appearance and behavior. Components from AWT and Swing can be mixed, allowing you to add Swing support to existing AWT-based programs. For example, swing components such as JSlider, JButton and JCheckbox could be used in the same program with standard AWT labels, textfields and scrollbars. You could subclass the existing Swing UI, model, or change listener classes without having to reinvent the entire implementation. Swing also has the ability to replace these objects on-the-fly.</p>
<table width="600" border="0" cellspacing="2" cellpadding="2">
<tbody>
<tr>
<td bgcolor="#fafadf">
<ul>
<li>100% Java implementation of components</li>
<li>Pluggable Look &amp; Feel</li>
<li>Lightweight components</li>
<li><strong>Uses MVC Architecture<br />
</strong> Model represents the data<br />
View as a visual representation of the data<br />
Controller takes input and translates it to changes in data</li>
<li><strong>Three parts </strong><br />
Component set (subclasses of JComponent)<br />
Support classes<br />
Interfaces</li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
<p>In Swing, classes that represent GUI components have names beginning with the letter J. Some examples are JButton, JLabel, and JSlider. Altogether there are more than 250 new classes and 75 interfaces in Swing  twice as many as in AWT.</p>
<p><strong style="text-decoration: underline;">Java Swing class hierarchy</strong></p>
<p>The class <strong style="font-weight: 400;">JComponent</strong>, descended directly from Container, is the root class for most of Swing&#8217;s user interface components.</p>
<p><img alt="" src="../images/java-swing.gif" width="610" height="325" /></p>
<p>Swing contains <strong style="font-weight: 400;">components</strong> that you&#8217;ll use to build a GUI. I am listing you some of the commonly used Swing components. To learn and understand these swing programs, AWT Programming knowledge <strong>is not</strong> required.</p>
<h1><span style="font-size: medium;">Java Swing Examples</span></h1>
<p><a onclick="javascript:pageTracker._trackPageview('/outgoing/www.wideskills.com');"  href="http://www.wideskills.com"><img class="aligncenter size-full wp-image-569" alt="Wideskills" src="http://www.javabeginner.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/02/Wideskiils-4.png" width="486" height="147" /></a></p>
<p class="style4">Below is a java swing code for the traditional Hello World program.</p>
<p>Basically, the idea behind this Hello World program is to learn how to create a java program, compile and run it. To create your java source code you can use any editor( Text pad/Edit plus are my favorites) or you can use an IDE like <strong style="font-weight: 400;">Eclipse</strong>.</p>
<pre class="wp-code-highlight prettyprint">
import javax.swing.JFrame;
import javax.swing.JLabel;

//import statements
//Check if window closes automatically. Otherwise add suitable code
public class HelloWorldFrame extends JFrame {

	public static void main(String args[]) {
		new HelloWorldFrame();
	}
	HelloWorldFrame() {
		JLabel jlbHelloWorld = new JLabel(&quot;Hello World&quot;);
		add(jlbHelloWorld);
		this.setSize(100, 100);
		// pack();
		setVisible(true);
	}
}
</pre>
<p class="style4">Output</p>
<p class="style9"><img alt="" src="../images/java-swing-example.jpg" width="140" height="100" /></p>
<p><span class="style14"><strong>Note: </strong><span class="style13">Below are some links to java swing tutorials that forms a helping hand to get started with java programming swing.</span></span></p>
<ul>
<li><span class="style5">JPanel</span> is Swing&#8217;s version of the AWT class Panel and uses the same default layout, FlowLayout. JPanel is descended directly from JComponent.</li>
<li><a href="http://www.javabeginner.com/java-swing/java-jframe-class-example"><span class="style6"><strong><span class="style6">JFrame</span></strong></span></a> is Swing&#8217;s version of Frame and is descended directly from that class. The components added to the frame are referred to as its contents; these are managed by the contentPane. To add a component to a JFrame, we must use its contentPane instead.</li>
<li><a href="http://www.javabeginner.com/java-swing/java-jinternalframe-class-example"><span class="style6"><strong><span class="style6">JInternalFrame</span></strong></span></a> is confined to a visible area of a container it is placed in. It can be iconified , maximized and layered.</li>
<li><a href="http://www.javabeginner.com/java-swing/java-jwindow-class-example"><span class="style6"><strong><span class="style6">JWindow</span> </strong></span></a>is Swing&#8217;s version of Window and is descended directly from that class. Like Window, it uses BorderLayout by default.</li>
<li><span class="style5">JDialog</span> is Swing&#8217;s version of Dialog and is descended directly from that class. Like Dialog, it uses BorderLayout by default. Like JFrame and JWindow,<br />
JDialog contains a rootPane hierarchy including a contentPane, and it allows layered and glass panes. All dialogs are modal, which means the current<br />
thread is blocked until user interaction with it has been completed. JDialog class is intended as the basis for creating custom dialogs; however, some<br />
of the most common dialogs are provided through static methods in the class JOptionPane.</li>
<li><a href="http://www.javabeginner.com/java-swing/java-jlabel-class-example"><span class="style6"><strong><span class="style6">JLabel</span></strong></span></a>, descended from JComponent, is used to create text labels.</li>
<li>The abstract class AbstractButton extends class JComponent and provides a foundation for a family of button classes, including<span class="style6"><span class="style6"><strong>JButton</strong></span>.</span></li>
<li><a href="http://www.javabeginner.com/java-swing/java-jtextfield-class-example"><span class="style6"><strong><span class="style6">JTextField</span></strong></span></a> allows editing of a single line of text. New features include the ability to justify the text left, right, or center, and to set the text&#8217;s font.</li>
<li><a href="http://www.javabeginner.com/java-swing/java-jpasswordfield-class-example"><span class="style6"><strong><span class="style6">JPasswordField</span></strong></span></a> (a direct subclass of JTextField) you can suppress the display of input. Each character entered can be replaced by an echo character.<br />
This allows confidential input for passwords, for example. By default, the echo character is the asterisk, *.</li>
<li><span class="style6"><strong><a href="http://www.javabeginner.com/java-swing/java-jtextarea-class-example"><span class="style6">JTextArea</span></a> </strong></span>allows editing of multiple lines of text. JTextArea can be used in conjunction with class JScrollPane to achieve scrolling. The underlying <span class="style6"> <strong style="font-weight: 400;">JScrollPane</strong></span> can be forced to always or never have either the vertical or horizontal scrollbar;<br />
JButton is a component the user clicks to trigger a specific action.</li>
<li><a href="http://www.javabeginner.com/java-swing/java-jbutton-class-example"><span class="style6"><strong><span class="style6">JRadioButton</span></strong></span></a> is similar to JCheckbox, except for the default icon for each class. A set of radio buttons can be associated as a group in which only<br />
one button at a time can be selected.</li>
<li><span class="style6"><strong><a href="http://www.javabeginner.com/java-swing/java-jcheckbox-class-example"><span class="style6">JCheckBox</span></a> </strong></span>is not a member of a checkbox group. A checkbox can be selected and deselected, and it also displays its current state.</li>
<li><a href="http://www.javabeginner.com/java-swing/java-jcombobox-class-example"><span class="style6"><strong><span class="style6">JComboBox</span> </strong></span></a>is like a drop down box. You can click a drop-down arrow and select an option from a list. For example, when the component has focus,<br />
pressing a key that corresponds to the first character in some entry&#8217;s name selects that entry. A vertical scrollbar is used for longer lists.</li>
<li><span class="style6"><strong><a href="http://www.javabeginner.com/java-swing/java-jlist-class-example"><span class="style6">JList</span></a> </strong></span>provides a scrollable set of items from which one or more may be selected. JList can be populated from an Array or Vector. JList does not<br />
support scrolling directly, instead, the list must be associated with a scrollpane. The view port used by the scroll pane can also have a user-defined<br />
border. JList actions are handled using ListSelectionListener.</li>
<li><a href="http://www.javabeginner.com/java-swing/java-jtabbedpane-class-example"><span class="style6"><strong><span class="style6">JTabbedPane</span></strong></span> </a>contains a tab that can have a tool tip and a mnemonic, and it can display both text and an image.</li>
<li><a href="http://www.javabeginner.com/java-swing/java-jtoolbar-class-example"><span class="style6"><strong><span class="style6">JToolbar</span></strong></span> </a>contains a number of components whose type is usually some kind of button which can also include separators to group related components<br />
within the toolbar.</li>
<li><a href="http://www.javabeginner.com/java-swing/java-flowlayout-class-example"><span class="style6"><strong><span class="style6">FlowLayout</span></strong></span></a> when used arranges swing components from left to right until there&#8217;s no more space available. Then it begins a new row below it and moves<br />
from left to right again. Each component in a FlowLayout gets as much space as it needs and no more.</li>
<li><span class="style6"><strong><a href="http://www.javabeginner.com/java-swing/java-borderlayout-class-example"><span class="style6">BorderLayout</span></a> </strong></span>places swing components in the North, South, East, West and center of a container. You can add horizontal and vertical gaps between<br />
the areas.</li>
<li><a href="http://www.javabeginner.com/java-swing/java-gridlayout-class-example"><span class="style6"><strong><span class="style6">GridLayout</span></strong></span></a> is a layout manager that lays out a container&#8217;s components in a rectangular grid. The container is divided into equal-sized rectangles,<br />
and one component is placed in each rectangle.</li>
<li><a href="http://www.javabeginner.com/java-swing/java-gridbaglayout-class-example"><span class="style6"><strong><span class="style6">GridBagLayout</span></strong></span></a> is a layout manager that lays out a container&#8217;s components in a grid of cells with each component occupying one or more cells,<br />
called its display area. The display area aligns components vertically and horizontally, without requiring that the components be of the same size.</li>
<li><span class="style6"><strong><a href="http://www.javabeginner.com/java-swing/java-jmenu-class-example"><span class="style6">JMenubar</span></a> </strong></span>can contain several JMenu&#8217;s. Each of the JMenu&#8217;s can contain a series of JMenuItem &#8216;s that you can select. Swing provides support for<br />
pull-down and popup menus.</li>
<li><a href="http://www.javabeginner.com/java-swing/java-scrollable-popup-menu"><span class="style6"><strong><span class="style6">Scrollable JPopupMenu</span></strong></span></a> is a scrollable popup menu that can be used whenever we have so many items in a popup menu that exceeds the screen visible height.<br />
<h3>Java Swing Projects</h3>
</li>
<li><span class="style6"><strong><a href="http://www.javabeginner.com/java-swing/java-swing-calculator"><span class="style6">Java Swing Calculator</span></a> </strong></span>developed using Java Swing. It is a basic four-function calculator java program source code.</li>
<li><a href="http://www.javabeginner.com/java-swing/java-swing-address-book"><span class="style6"><strong><span class="style6">Java Swing Address</span></strong></span></a> Book demonstrates how to create a simple free address book program using java swing and jdbc. Also you will learn to use<br />
the following swing components like Jbuttons, JFrames, JTextFields and Layout Manager (GridBagLayout).</li>
</ul>
